<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Surviving_aircraft">Surviving aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Hurricane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Surviving aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_mkiic_of_the_bbmf_arp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1058" data-file-width="1706" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Hurricane_mkiic_of_the_bbmf_arp.jpg/220px-Hurricane_mkiic_of_the_bbmf_arp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Hurricane_mkiic_of_the_bbmf_arp.jpg/330px-Hurricane_mkiic_of_the_bbmf_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Hurricane_mkiic_of_the_bbmf_arp.jpg/440px-Hurricane_mkiic_of_the_bbmf_arp.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_mkiic_of_the_bbmf_arp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The last of the 14,583 Hurricanes built, s/n <i><a href="/wiki/Hawker_Hurricane_PZ865" title="Hawker Hurricane PZ865">PZ865</a></i>, . A Mk IIc version, originally known as "The Last of the Many" and owned by Hawker, this aircraft is now flown by the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain_Memorial_Flight" title="Battle of Britain Memorial Flight">Battle of Britain Memorial Flight</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_surviving_Hawker_Hurricanes" title="List of surviving Hawker Hurricanes">List of surviving Hawker Hurricanes</a></div>
<p>Of more than 14,583 Hurricanes that were built,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aholm_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-aholm-166">[155]</a></sup> only 12 (including three Sea Hurricanes) are in airworthy condition worldwide, although many other non-flying examples survive in various air museums.</p>
<h2><span id="Specifications_(Hurricane_Mk.IIC)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications_.28Hurricane_Mk.IIC.29">Specifications (Hurricane Mk.IIC)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Hurricane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Specifications (Hurricane Mk.IIC)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SmithsonianHawkerHurricane.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="291" data-file-width="600" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/SmithsonianHawkerHurricane.jpg/220px-SmithsonianHawkerHurricane.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/SmithsonianHawkerHurricane.jpg/330px-SmithsonianHawkerHurricane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/SmithsonianHawkerHurricane.jpg/440px-SmithsonianHawkerHurricane.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SmithsonianHawkerHurricane.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Hawker Hurricane on display at the <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="National Air and Space Museum">National Air and Space Museum</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Udvar-Hazy_Center" title="Udvar-Hazy Center">Udvar-Hazy Center</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p style="font-size: 90%; margin:0; padding: .2em"><i>Data from</i> <i>Jane's Fighting Aircraft of World War II</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jane_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-jane-167">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>General characteristics</b></span></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Crew:</b> 1</li>
<li><b>Length:</b> 32 ft 3 in (9.84 m)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Wingspan" title="Wingspan">Wingspan</a>:</b> 40 ft 0 in (12.19 m)</li>
<li><b>Height:</b> 13 ft 1½ in (4.0 m)</li>
<li><b>Wing area:</b> 257.5 ft² (23.92 m²)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Manufacturer%27s_empty_weight" title="Manufacturer's empty weight">Empty weight</a>:</b> 5,745 lb (2,605 kg)</li>
<li><b>Loaded weight:</b> 7,670 lb (3,480 kg)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Maximum_takeoff_weight" title="Maximum takeoff weight">Max. takeoff weight</a>:</b> 8,710 lb (3,950 kg)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Aircraft_engine" title="Aircraft engine">Powerplant</a>:</b> 1 × <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Merlin" title="Rolls-Royce Merlin">Rolls-Royce Merlin</a> XX liquid-cooled V-12, 1,185 hp (883 kW) at 21,000 ft (6,400 m)</li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>Performance</b></span></p>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/V_speeds#Regulatory_V-speeds" title="V speeds">Maximum speed</a>:</b> 340 mph (547 km/h) at 21,000 ft (6,400 m) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[N 12]</a></sup></li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Range_(aeronautics)" title="Range (aeronautics)">Range</a>:</b> 600 mi (965 km)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Ceiling_(aeronautics)" title="Ceiling (aeronautics)">Service ceiling</a>:</b> 36,000 ft (10,970 m)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Rate_of_climb" title="Rate of climb">Rate of climb</a>:</b> 2,780 ft/min (14.1 m/s)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Wing_loading" title="Wing loading">Wing loading</a>:</b> 29.8 lb/ft² (121.9 kg/m²)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Power-to-weight_ratio" title="Power-to-weight ratio">Power/mass</a>:</b> 0.15 hp/lb (0.25 kW/kg)</li>
</ul>
<p><span style="font-size: 120%;"><b>Armament</b></span><br/></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Guns:</b> 4 × 20 mm (.79 in) <a href="/wiki/Hispano-Suiza_HS.404" title="Hispano-Suiza HS.404">Hispano Mk II</a> cannon</li>
<li><b>Bombs:</b> 2 × 250 or 500 lb (110 or 230 kg) bombs</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Hurricane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hawker_Hurricane&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-49">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Mould was shot down on 1 October 1941 by Italian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macchi_MC.202" title="Macchi MC.202">Macchi MC.202s</a> north of <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and declared "<a href="/wiki/Missing_in_action" title="Missing in action">missing in action</a>".</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Heinkel He 112 was never operational in France.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-56">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">J. B. Parnall was the first RAF flight commander to be killed in action during the war.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-58">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Australian ace <a href="/wiki/Les_Clisby" title="Les Clisby">Les Clisby</a> was credited with 16 individual air victories, one shared and one not confirmed. Postwar research reduced his score to nine individual kills and three shared. According to some sources, he was killed on 15 May 1940.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-76">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This was the pilot's term for the Boost Cut-Out Control which was adjacent to the throttle lever.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-77">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Gleed rose through the ranks to become a wing commander flying Spitfire VBs over North Africa; he was shot down and killed by <i><a href="/wiki/Oberleutnant" title="Oberleutnant">Oberleutnant</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Ernst-Wilhelm_Reinert" title="Ernst-Wilhelm Reinert">Ernst-Wilhelm Reinert</a> on 16 April 1943. Gleed was credited with 15 victories.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-104">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As far as can be determined, no Messerschmitt Bf 110 crashes on land for 16 August 1940 can be attributed to Nicholson, although Nicholson himself believed the 110 crashed into the sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[97]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-114">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This was code-named Operation <i>Hurry</i>. These aircraft were flown off the carrier <a href="/wiki/HMS_Argus_(I49)" title="HMS Argus (I49)">HMS <i>Argus</i></a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-124"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-124">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Soviet Hurricanes were fuelled with 95 octane avgas, not the 100 Octane fuel that the Merlin XX was designed to use.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-126"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-126">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Soviet pilot Nikolai G. Golodnikov remembered: "The Hurricane’s engine was powerful, but it couldn’t stand long periods of work at maximum regimes and would quickly break down. The engine worked very clean, it had exhaust stacks and flame suppressors, mounted like mufflers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[N 9]</a></sup> This was very comfortable as the flames did not blind the pilot. Our planes were much worse in this respect. But at negative G-forces the engine chocked. There was no compensating tank. This was very bad because we had to execute any manoeuvre with positive G-forces. It had a very thick wing profile and poor acceleration characteristics. It was not slow in responding to the control stick, but everything happened smoothly, slowly. It had good lifting strength and was very good in horizontal manoeuvrability. But the Hurricane was very poor in vertical manoeuvre, due to thick wing profile. We mostly tried to impose a battle in the horizontal plane and would not go into a vertical one. The Hurricane burned rapidly — and to cinders like a match — as it had <a href="/wiki/Duralumin" title="Duralumin">dural</a> covering only on the tail and wings, the rest was <a href="/wiki/Percale" title="Percale">percale</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[116]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Malta: The Spitfire Year 1942</i> records 28 Sea Hurricane victories against eight losses during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Harpoon_(1942)" title="Operation Harpoon (1942)">Operation Harpoon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Pedestal" title="Operation Pedestal">Operation Pedestal</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-168"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-168">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">320 mph (510 km/h) at 19,700 ft (6,000 m) with two 250 lb (110 kg) bombs</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
